The Clipper Arrives for Test Flight in Midway: Using Radio as a Compass; Advances Against the Wind 81

Alameda, USA. Pan American Airlines dispatched the large aircraft *Oriental Clipper* this afternoon at 3:00, heading to Midway Island via Honolulu. According to the company, the aircraft will encounter clouds and heavy rain 250 miles off the Pacific coast. However, this type of weather is actually what is desired for this flight, because in this way, it can be tested whether the newly invented radio navigation function can guide the aircraft. The aircraft tried to fly last week but stopped because the weather was too good. The aircraft will stop briefly in Honolulu and then fly to Midway Island. As for the personnel on board, they are the same as on the last flight to Honolulu, but without mail or cargo. (National News, 12th)

Alameda, USA. The giant aircraft *Oriental Clipper*, which was flown to Honolulu by Moesick in April, departed again today with Mr. Moesick leading a crew of five, with Midway Island as the destination. The aircraft is carrying 3,000 gallons of gasoline and 300 gallons of regular oil. According to a radio message from the aircraft after departure, the aircraft is currently encountering headwinds of 20 miles per hour, but is still able to advance at a speed of 112 miles per hour. A later message stated that the aircraft is currently encountering heavy fog. (National News Agency, 12th)

San Francisco. Pan American's large airship, the *Clipper*, departed from here at midnight, heading to Midway Island, about 4,000 miles north of the Hawaiian Islands, to test the airship's strength in unstable conditions. Knowing that the weather ahead would be unfavorable, the airship will make a brief stop in Hawaii, about halfway between here and Midway Island. Four hours after departure, a radio message stated that everything was going smoothly. (Reuters, 13th)

The Japanese Cabinet Investigation Bureau Holds Its First Meeting: Prime Minister Okada Attends and Delivers an Instruction Speech 82

However, the desired results cannot be achieved with the existing system alone. The Cabinet Investigation Bureau was established after careful discussions. The duty of the Investigation Bureau is to investigate important policies, and during the investigation, it is necessary to fully examine the interests of all parties and integrate and unify them from a national perspective. The purpose of establishing a system of participation is also to exert this function. At this important moment in the political situation, I earnestly hope that you will do your best for the country. Armistice Agreement Signed Between Bolivia and Paraguay, Ceasefire Within 24 Hours, Neutral Countries Form Commission 89

(Buenos Aires) The Bolivia-Paraguay armistice agreement was signed this afternoon, stipulating a ceasefire within 24 hours. The reason for needing 24 hours is that the 375-mile front line must be notified of the ceasefire one by one. (Reuters Telegram on the 12th)

(Buenos Aires) According to the armistice agreement of the Chaco peace talks, the troops of Bolivia and Paraguay should cease fire immediately on the 12th, so that a military commission of neutral countries can survey the area and separate the warring armies by a considerable distance. This commission, organized by military officers from Argentina, Brazil, Chile, Uruguay, and the United States, was established and flew to the Chaco battlefield last night. (Havas Telegram on the 12th)

(Buenos Aires) Regarding the armistice agreement of the Chaco peace talks, it was officially signed here at 12:32 this afternoon by representatives of Bolivia and Paraguay together with representatives of various neutral countries. The agreement stipulates that the foreign ministers of Bolivia and Paraguay request all mediating countries to immediately convene a peace conference with the following objectives: (1) To enact laws to allow the governments of the parties concerned to ratify this agreement within ten days. (2) To resolve various practical issues in implementing this agreement. (3) To find a way for Bolivia and Paraguay to directly negotiate the territorial dispute in the Chaco region. If direct negotiations fail, it will be submitted to the International Court of Justice in The Hague for adjudication. (4) To exchange prisoners of war between Bolivia and Paraguay and send them back to their respective countries. (5) To stipulate transportation and navigation systems. (6) To conclude various economic agreements. (7) To organize an international commission to determine responsibility for violating this agreement. (8) Both sides will cease fire for 12 days so that a military commission of neutral countries can survey the area and separate the armies of Bolivia and Paraguay by a considerable distance. The ceasefire will begin at midnight on the evening that the commission arrives at the front line. After the isolation zone between the two armies is demarcated, the military commission of neutral countries will be responsible for its management. (Havas Telegram on the 12th)

Record of Hu Hanmin's Departure 93

Guangzhou Correspondence: Mr. Hu Hanmin, who has been in Hong Kong for a long time, has been away from the political stage for quite some time since going south. Although he occasionally expresses his opinions on the current situation in Hong Kong, he only contributes opinions on Southwest political affairs and has never set foot in Guangzhou. Therefore, both the northern and southern political circles attach great importance to Hu's remarks. The news of Hu's departure abroad has been widely spread for a long time. However, he suffered from high blood pressure, which caused him to suspend his trip. In March, after a doctor's examination, his blood pressure has recently dropped back to 170 degrees, and his health has slightly improved. Therefore, he decided to go abroad for recuperation and take a breath of fresh air, which is the reason for Hu's departure this time. After Hu decided on the date of departure, the Southwest political circles went to Hong Kong one after another to meet Hu and discuss the current situation and ask for instructions on future plans. Those who arrived in Hong Kong first included Zou Lu, member of the Southwest Political Affairs Committee and President of Zhongshan University, Chen Zhongfu, member of the Central Committee, and Chen Rong, Secretary-General of the Political Affairs Committee. On the 8th, those who visited Hu included Li Zongren, Commander-in-Chief of the Gui Army and member of the Southwest Political Affairs Committee, Lin Yizhong, Director of the Civil Affairs Department of Guangdong Province, Qu Fangpu, Director of the Finance Department, Liu Jiwen, Mayor of Guangzhou, Yang Xiji, Director of the Audit Office of the Political Affairs Committee, Li Luchao, member of the Provincial Government, Zhang Renmin, Chief of Staff of the Gui Army, Tan Huiquan of the Provincial Party Committee, and Lu Sizeng, President of Dongqin University. The officials visited Hu in turn and asked for instructions on everything. Therefore, since the 7th, Hu's residence in Hong Kong has been crowded with visitors. Hu either had intimate talks with comrades or just socialized briefly. After Hu's residence packed up, he first transported his luggage to the Italian郵船"Conte Verde" on the evening of the 8th. On the afternoon of the 9th, at 4:00 PM, Mr. Hu, together with his wife and daughter Mulan, as well as attendants Cheng Tiangu (former Mayor of Guangzhou), doctor Chen Yiping, secretary Shi Yangchong, female secretary Zhong Huizhong, and attendants Huang Lianzhong and Liang Xingling, a group of nine people, boarded the Italian郵船"Conte Verde" by ferry from Hong Kong. Li Zongren, Lin Yizhong, Zou Lu, Liu Jiwen, Li Jishen, Qu Fangpu, Chen Jiayou, Yang Xiji, and Tan Huiquan all personally sent them off to the Italian郵船. When Hu was about to leave, he did not talk about political diplomacy to the outside world, only saying that his own views would not change due to the transfer of time and place. Hu was wearing a white long coat and glasses on the ship. Those who served him were his daughter Mulan and Ms. Zhong Huizhong. Hu talked with the send-offs for a while, then took a photo with Li Zongren, Zou Lu, Lin Yizhong, Qu Fangpu, Gan Jiehou, Liu Jiwen, Hu Mulan, Hu's wife, and Zhong Huizhong. The send-offs then bid farewell. After Hu was also tired, he went to rest in the P-class cabin of the ship. After everyone dispersed, Jiang Guangnai, Jiang Tingkai, Tan Qixiu, and Shen Guanghan also rushed to see him off, and talked with Hu for about three minutes before shaking hands and leaving. It was already 5:00 PM. With a whistle, the ship had already set sail, and the military and political circles of Guangzhou who came to see him off returned to the province by evening train. It is said that Hu's departure this time will first go to Italy, then to Switzerland, to stay for recuperation temporarily, and the date of return is undecided. Chen Shiyi, a poet from Fujian, visited Hu before he left Hong Kong and had a close exchange with Hu. Before leaving, Hu wrote a poem entitled "Again in the Rhyme of the Old Poet Shi Yi to Bid Farewell to Comrades," which says: "Luo Xi has a saying about a strange man, not disappointed that this old man knows when parting, the country is in distress and can be regarded as Jin and Song, the poem is foolish and inconvenient to go to Chai Can, those who follow me are in agreement with the Tao, and there are still people who calculate it to the south, and try to take my child for thousands of miles, and ten years of old things are worth deep talks." (June 10th)

Southwest Civil Aviation Expands Equipment, Meteorological Station Established in Zhaoqing 94

Southwest Civil Aviation has recently expanded its equipment in various stations in Guangdong and Guangxi. Starting from Shipai in Guangzhou, wireless stations have been set up in Wuzhou, Nanning, Longzhou, Maoming, Qiongzhou, and Beihai. Recently, all stations have been uniformly retrofitted with both long-wave and short-wave transceivers for use in case of weather changes. Moreover, long-distance flights between Guangdong and Guangxi cannot ensure safety without weather reports. Therefore, a meteorological station has been established in Zhaoqing, the central station between Guangdong and Guangxi, to report on the weather. The establishment of this station has made civil aviation aircraft traveling to and from Guangdong and Guangxi more convenient. As a result, important figures from Guangdong and Guangxi travel between the two provinces by civil aviation aircraft. On the first of this month, Gui Army Chief of Staff Ye Qi was ordered to come to Guangdong to meet Li Zongren and Chen Jitang of the Guangdong military authorities. The civil aviation aircraft that Ye took arrived safely in the provincial capital on the afternoon of the 1st. On the 2nd, he went to Mapenggang in Dongshan to visit Li Zongren, reported on the military affairs of Guangxi Province, and described in detail the situation of the troops stationed on the border between Guangxi and Guizhou, as well as the situation after the communist bandits on the border between Guizhou fled to Sichuan. He then visited Chen Jitang, and Chen asked about the situation on the border of Guizhou. Ye and Chen also had matters to discuss. They returned to discuss in detail several times in the past few days. Chen hosted a banquet for Ye. The guests and hosts had a very pleasant conversation. On the morning of the 5th, Ye accompanied Li Zongren to Meihuacun to visit Chen Jitang and discussed various military affairs in detail again. A satisfactory solution was reached at 11:00 AM. It is reported that Ye's mission in Guangdong has been completed, and he left Guangdong on the 6th to return to Guangxi to report.

Two-Hubei Supervisory Envoy Office Officially Established in Hubei, Changsha Office Temporarily Not Established, Gao Yihan Immediately Goes to Various Places for Inspection 95

Hankou Correspondence: Gao Yihan, Supervisory Envoy of the Supervisory Yuan in Hubei, after taking office in Beijing, led his staff to Hankou to prepare for the establishment of the office. On the 12th, the Supervisory Envoy Office was officially established at No. 26, Houbu Street, Wuchang, and the seal was put into use and office work began. He reported to the Supervisory Yuan and sent letters to various agencies for information. The organization of the office strives for simplicity, with only a secretariat and one or two sections. On the 12th, Xie Yungao was first appointed as the secretary, and the remaining staff will be fully announced on the 13th. Mr. Gao said that the office is a new establishment, and in order to make all sectors of society understand the powers of the Supervisory Envoy, he is scheduled to receive the press this week and report on everything. The original plan to establish an office in Changsha has now been abandoned. According to Mr. Gao, after the office affairs are arranged, he will go to the supervisory area under his jurisdiction for inspections to know the people's suffering and the gains and losses of officialdom, so as to fully exercise the power of supervision and live up to the expectations of the Supervisory Yuan and the people. The inspection regulations are announced as follows: Article 1: These regulations are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 6 of the Supervisory Yuan Organization Law. Article 2: The Supervisory Envoy shall conduct inspections within the supervisory area to which they are assigned. Article 3: The impeachment case submitted by the Supervisory Envoy shall be in writing, but in case of emergency, it may be submitted by telegram first, and then the facts shall be prepared. The impeachment case submitted by the Supervisory Envoy shall be subject to the procedures of Article 5 of the Impeachment Law. Article 4: In exercising his powers, the Supervisory Envoy may inquire of the official agencies and other public institutions within the supervisory area to which he is assigned, or investigate archives and registers. If there are any questions, the responsible person shall be responsible for providing honest answers. Article 5: If the Supervisory Envoy believes that the illegal and derelict conduct of public officials in the supervisory area to which they are assigned is serious and requires urgent relief, in addition to filing an impeachment case, he may also directly notify the competent leader to give urgent relief. If the competent leader does not take urgent relief measures upon receiving the above-mentioned notice, he shall be held responsible when the impeached person is punished. Article 6: The Supervisory Envoy may accept the people's reports of illegal or derelict conduct of public officials, but shall not answer them. Article 7: The Supervisory Envoy shall report the supervisory situation to the Supervisory Yuan at any time and pay attention to the following matters: 1. Matters relating to the facilities of official agencies and public institutions within the supervisory area to which they are assigned. 2. Matters relating to the actions of public officials within the supervisory area to which they are assigned. 3. Matters relating to the people's suffering and grievances within the supervisory area to which they are assigned. Article 8: The Supervisory Envoy shall establish a Supervisory Envoy Office within the supervisory area. The Supervisory Envoy Office shall have one to two secretaries, two section chiefs, two assigned clerks, four to six appointed staff members, and one to two hired advisors. The general rules for handling affairs of the Supervisory Envoy Office shall be determined separately. Article 9: The Supervisory Envoy and his staff shall not accept local supplies or gifts. Article 10: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. (June 12)

Current Situation of Qimen Tea Production and Sales: This Year's Sales Price Plummets, Severely Impacting Farmers and Businesses 96

Correspondence from Poyuan: Qimen, with its limited land and mountainous terrain, boasts special local products. Aside from porcelain clay, tea is the most significant product. Its superior quality has long held a leading position in the global market. The livelihood of farmers largely depends on it. Therefore, the prosperity or decline of the tea market determines the economic well-being of the Qimen rural areas. In the past five years, the global consumption of Qihong (Qimen red tea) in various countries has suffered from economic hardship. Preference has been given to cheaper options, coupled with the dumping of Indian and Javanese black tea at low prices. The sales price of Qimen tea has plummeted. The losses suffered by tea merchants are especially pronounced this past year. Although the output of new tea this year is reported to be poor, tea firms have tried hard to improve their processing methods. However, the sales and market performance of the first two batches of boxed tea shipped to Shanghai not only remain sluggish, but are even worse than before. Tea merchants are frowning, feeling that they have exhausted all means of recovery. The misfortune seems to be intensifying. For example, more than 4,000 boxes of tea from 22 tea firms were lost when they sank in Poyang Lake last month, resulting in losses of over 400,000 yuan. Tea merchants have barely caught their breath, and are already facing another heavy blow. The old losses and new wounds are truly overwhelming. Whether the market can turn towards a smooth path in the future is currently difficult to predict. The following is a detailed investigation of the current situation of Qimen tea production and sales this year:

Reduced Production Volume: In previous years, the production volume of Qimen tea was approximately over 30,000 dan, yielding about 60,000 boxes of dried tea (excluding what is collected by Fuliang). According to statistics from the Anhui Construction Department in 1930, the output was 22,005 dan, yielding over 40,000 boxes of dried tea. Last year's tax statistics also showed 38,500 boxes. This year's production volume, up to the end of the spring tea harvest (excluding Zi tea), is estimated by various firms to be only over 26,000 boxes. After deducting the 4,000 boxes that sank in Poyang Lake last month, the total is no more than 22,000 boxes. This is a significant difference compared to the production volume of previous years. Even compared to last year's output, it is a reduction of over 16,000 boxes. The reasons for this reduction are: (1) Farmers, seeing the recent oversupply of tea, leading to a supply exceeding demand and low market prices, with sales prices not covering costs, have not paid attention to tea tree cultivation, allowing them to become mostly barren, leading to a reduction in production volume. (2) Last year's severe drought in summer and autumn, and the lack of snow in winter, caused the tea gardens to dry up. The tea roots did not receive rain nourishment for a long time, resulting in weak growth. (3) The production volume of Zi tea (i.e., summer tea) accounts for approximately two-tenths of the spring tea. This year's spring tea sales price was weak, and no farmers harvested or processed it. Tea firms also stopped purchasing it. Due to the above three reasons, the production volume of Qimen tea this year is even more reduced.

Tea Firms Tightening Up: In the past, Qimen tea's prosperity was due to the large sales volume in Europe and America, with market prices rising year by year. The number of tea estates and processing factories also increased accordingly. In 1930, there were over 90 tea firms in the entire county. In 1931, it increased to 114. In 1932, it increased further to 182. Last year, the number decreased by over 20. This year, there are a total of 137 firms opening for business (including over 20 cooperatives), which is over 30 fewer than before. The reason for this reduction is that the original tea firms have suffered years of losses, and their capital is exhausted, making it difficult to start a business. Even the firms that resumed business this year have mostly tightened up their operations and strived to reduce costs to avoid further losses. This approach seems to be unanimous among the firms. However, in reality, the situation is quite different. When new tea comes onto the market, the competitive spirit of a few firms is always difficult to eliminate. Some are lukewarm, others are enthusiastic; some suppress, others raise prices. The mountain price is still difficult to standardize, leading to an increase in costs. In addition, this year, many firms have a poor harvest, forming a situation where demand exceeds supply. In previous years, each firm's number of boxes was mostly over 200 to 300 boxes. This year, the average firm only has 100 to 200 boxes. Only a few dozen firms have 200 boxes. Although the number of boxes has decreased, the firm's expenses cannot be reduced accordingly. Each firm spends between 2,000 and 3,000 yuan. In addition, there are more than 2 yuan in taxes per box (this year is several times higher than last year), 5 to 6 yuan in shipping costs, and Shanghai warehouse rent, insurance, and commissions. In total, the cost of the first batch of boxed tea is approximately between 170 and 180 yuan per dan. The cost has increased invisibly. The tea firms' initial intention to tighten up operations, reduce costs, and avoid losses has now become uncertain.

Farmers' Suffering: Qimen farmers, who cultivate rice for their own consumption, do not have enough food. Their annual income from local products, except for the mining of porcelain clay for sale in Jingdezhen, all depend on the abundant tea harvest and good prices to alleviate their impoverished lives. In the prosperous years of Qihong, the tea prices earned by mountain farmers were higher than those in Wuyuan, Xiuning, and Shexian. This is because Wuyuan and Xiuning green tea is dried once and sold, with the highest price per dan being only 70 to 80 yuan. Qimen tea is not dried once. The core contains moisture, forming semi-dried tea buds, which are sold to tea firms. The highest price per 100 jin can reach 120 to 130 yuan, which is only half the weight of dried green tea. If two are combined into one, the price is also doubled. This only refers to the total income from the sale of tea leaves by Qimen mountain farmers. Calculating the labor and food costs for tea picking, the actual income is not substantial. This is because most Qimen tea farmers do not pick the tea themselves. They need to hire outside workers for picking and processing. Even if we calculate the average price of rough black tea at approximately 20 yuan per dan this year, it is only enough to cover the cost of labor. The income earned by the producers is very meager. Also, if we calculate the county's production volume of 25,000 dan this year, the tea farmers' income is only 750,000 yuan. After deducting half for labor costs, only 375,000 yuan flows into the mountain farmers of the entire county. The income of the entire rural area is limited. A drop in the bucket is of no help to the parched land. Although the Pingli Tea Improvement Center and the National Economic Commission have sent personnel to guide the organization of tea transportation and sales cooperatives to alleviate the suffering of farmers, each village is limited to a few households. Members are farmers who own tea production. All equipment is trained and instructed by the technicians from the center and the Economic Commission. Funds are borrowed from the Shanghai Bank. The authorities are sincerely trying to help, and the methods are not without merit. However, there are still a few unscrupulous individuals who manipulate or falsely organize cooperatives, secretly using their old tricks to exploit tea farmers. Therefore, before the cooperatives have a solid organization and significant results for the individual benefits of tea farmers, it is difficult for tea farmers to obtain practical benefits and universal coverage.

Financial Insufficiency: The prosperity of Qimen tea firms in the past was due to high overseas sales prices and the availability of ample credit. Seven or eight years ago, Shanghai tea firms, in order to compete for a larger share of the boxed tea, were mostly lenient and generous in lending money to customers. Each year, the tea firms lent tea money to tea firms, often reaching around 2 million yuan. In recent years, due to poor overseas sales, tea firms have accumulated losses, and the losses suffered by the firms have been substantial. After discussions among the firms, new regulations were formulated to prevent further losses. After mutual compliance and implementation, the firms' loans to tea firms have been mostly tightened. Therefore, in recent years, most tea firms have felt that their own capital is weak, and it is not easy to obtain loans from firms. It is difficult to dance with short sleeves. They all suffer from the exhaustion of all resources. Last year, although the Four Provinces Farmers Bank sent personnel to Qimen to provide loans, the total amount lent in one month was only over 20,000 yuan, which was very meager. It still could not help to promote financial flexibility. This year, due to the Silver and Money Industry Bureau's tight control over lending, the sources of funds for each tea firm are increasingly scarce. The total amount of loans lent by each firm in Qimen this year is only over 800,000 yuan (the maximum loan amount per firm is 6,000 yuan, and the minimum is 3,000 yuan). Adding the tea firms' own capital of 30 to 40 percent, the total is only over 1.2 to 1.3 million yuan. This is only enough to circulate the huge amount of Qimen tea production of 50 to 60 thousand boxes. How can this be sufficient? Speaking of development is even more difficult.

Sluggish Sales Prices: Production and consumption are both indispensable. If there is production without a market, then there will be excessive expansion. The decline of Qimen tea today is due to the lack of smooth channels and the increasingly low market prices. If the market is small and the market price is high, operators can still benefit. If the market price is flat and does not hurt the capital, tea merchants can still support it. However, in recent years, both sales volume and market price have been declining. Even if tea firms have abundant capital, they cannot withstand repeated losses. Qimen tea is suffering from the pressure of sales prices. Everyone is exhausted and sinking into a deep abyss, unable to save themselves. Last year, tea merchants eagerly hoped that the overseas market would improve and slightly compensate for previous losses. However, when the new tea came onto the market, the sales market remained stagnant. In total, over 15,000 boxes of tea from Qimen and Fuliang were shipped to Shanghai last month. The top-grade Qigong was only priced at 165 yuan, and the rest ranged from 100 to 150 yuan, which was 40 yuan lower than last year. The Zhongzhuang was priced at 80 to 90 yuan, and the low-grade goods were priced at 70 to 50 yuan. The Huaxiang was priced at 24 yuan, which was 70% lower than before. Except for a slight intake from British firms, there were few transactions from Russian firms and other merchants. Although after the middle of last month, British firms received news of a large amount of Qimen tea sinking in Poyang Lake, their willingness to buy increased, and the market price rose by 5 to 6 yuan. The highest quality was raised back to 180 yuan. However, this market price only applied to a small number of tribute goods, ranging from 10 to 40 pieces. Calculating the cost, there was still a large loss. Even the principal of ordinary first tea costs 170 to 180 yuan. If the highest price is still losing money, others can be imagined. It is expected that the final result of Qimen tea this year is that the overall losses of merchants will not be lower than in previous years. (June 8)

Suzhou: Active Capture and Elimination of Locust Plague in the Four Rural Areas 97

The various rural areas of Suzhou have suffered from severe drought since entering summer, and are now showing signs of disaster. In the western rural area of Hengjing, a locust plague has broken out. The Wu County Magistrate has personally gone to the rural areas, along with the Party Headquarters Agricultural Department and other institutions, to direct the villagers to capture and eliminate the locusts. In recent days, over 1,000 jin have been captured. It was found that in the fields of Zhuang and other places in the rural area, only nymphs were initially found. In just five or six days, they developed into flying locusts. At the same time, in Niuyanjing and other places in the territory of Wujiang, locusts gathered on the ground, piling up more than a foot high. The villagers drove them to capture them. They covered the sky and the sun, and flocked to the Hengjing rural area of Suzhou, causing more to be captured between, and the more they captured, the more there were, and they could not win. In the towns of Yuexi and Nanku in Wujiang, a large number of locusts also flew into the territory of Suzhou, in groups of tens of millions, and have now spread to Xukou outside Xumen, and Guoxiang Chefang outside Fengmen. The city party once transferred a fire pump truck to the countryside to remove the locusts by spraying water, but the effect was not great. Although the locust catching bag made by the Agricultural School is extremely applicable, there are too many locusts, and it is too slow. Wujiang has also begun to contact Wu County to capture them together. Hengjing Jin District Chief Qian has already held a meeting to decide to change to large fishing nets, which will be spread on the fields at dawn. After an hour, the locusts will fly into the net, and then quickly collect them. In this way, dozens of pounds can be obtained in one net. They are capturing day and night, and are limited to cleaning up within three days. As soon as the drought appeared, the locust plague became a reality. Although the capture work is currently extremely tense, whether it can be completely captured and eliminated is still a question.

Wuxi: Three Industries Negotiate Grain Insurance 98

There are a total of twenty-seven grain storage and industry stores in Wuxi, which specialize in storing grain and other goods, and also operate mortgage businesses. The warehouse receipts issued are of excellent credit. Because the storage is safe and reliable, insurance has not been handled in the past, and there have been very few water and fire accidents. Recently, the storage industry has been considering handling insurance for the sake of consolidating business safety, and has negotiated with the Rice and Bean Bank and the two industries once. However, there are many types of grains and persimmons, and the amount of storage varies, which is different from the insurance of other goods, so it is difficult to have specific measures for a while. Later, the banking industry telegraphed and agreed with Shanghai China, Taiping, Anping, Baofeng, Taishan, Fengsheng, and other six insurance companies that are related to the industry to send representatives Dong Hanxi and Xiang Yuwu and other five people to Wuxi the day before yesterday to invite representatives from the storage, bank, and two industries to exchange opinions at the Bankers Association. After the negotiation, the following four principles were determined: (1) Each storage warehouse will insure the type of grain stored with the insurance company, assuming an integer, and the company will issue a policy as proof. (2) The insurance premium will be calculated by each warehouse sending a form with the actual amount insured on a daily basis to the insurance company for daily calculation. (3) In the event of an accident, the insurance will be paid according to the amount reported by the warehouse in the form. (4) In the future, each insurance company will set up a joint office in Wuxi in order to contact each other in case of an accident.

Changzhou: Abolition of Three Kinds of Harsh and Minor Taxes 99

Zhang Yipeng, a member of the Jiangsu Provincial Donation and Tax Supervision Committee, previously came to Changzhou to investigate harsh and minor taxes. It is now learned that Commissioner Zhang has drafted an investigation form and submitted it to the committee for discussion and approval. The items listed in the investigation form that should be abolished are: the meat shop cold meat tax, amounting to 2,200 yuan; the education miscellaneous tax, amounting to 1,698 yuan; and the public security miscellaneous tax, amounting to 300 yuan. The education miscellaneous tax and the public security miscellaneous tax have already been automatically deleted in the newly compiled budget for the 24th year, and there is no problem of resistance. The offset after the meat shop cold meat tax is abolished is subsidized by the Department of Finance in the amount of 40% of the stamp duty allocated by the Ministry. There are a total of nine kinds that are retained, such as damage, house police tax (merged into house tax), and public welfare tax. All have been automatically abolished. The remaining house tax, car tax, banquet tax, hotel tax, swimming tax, and advertising tax are six kinds that are still permitted by common practice and are considered to be temporarily retained.

Changshu: Merchants and Residents Demand Reduction of Rent 100

In recent years, the economy has declined, and all industries have withered. Therefore, the number of stores that have closed down is everywhere. The recession of commerce can be seen from this. Therefore, those who maintain the stores now are trying their best to save expenses. Now, the shops in the southeast gate area should have the necessity of reducing the rent due to the decline in business in recent years. Therefore, some of the shopkeepers have united to form a tenant union, demanding that the landlords reduce the rent by 30%. They are now in the process of contacting and signing, and will officially hold a meeting in the near future to decide on the implementation plan.

Haimen: Qidong Township Chief Arrested for Extortion 101

In the autumn of 1930, Qidong was harassed by bandits, and the people were restless. The villagers organized a self-defense corps to capture and kill several bandit leaders, and the bandit situation gradually subsided. However, recently, Yang Hankui, the township chief of Zhongqing Township in a certain district, colluded with the family members of the dead bandits and fabricated lies to the provincial and county governments to accuse the self-defense personnel who handled the matter that year, intending to extort money. When the people of each district learned of this, they were all indignant. They jointly presented the case to the Nantong District Commissioner's Office, which sent personnel to investigate and found that it was true. Yesterday, the county government was secretly ordered to send the police to arrest Yang. After questioning by Zhou Cheng, the secret member of the trial, Yang was ordered to be detained.

Jiangyin: Agriculture Director Acquitted of Embezzlement 102

When He Bukun, the former director of the Agricultural Extension Institute, handed over his duties on August 1 last year, the number of seedlings in the county nursery was found to be inconsistent with the number after the successor's detailed count. The Ministry of Construction checked and found that 210,000 seedlings were missing, worth more than 10,000 yuan, and ordered He Bukun to compensate. He suspected that the people's hearts were treacherous. He did not check in detail for a while, and was deceived. He sued the county government. The Ministry of Construction believed that the matter involved responsibility and was related to embezzlement, and transferred the entire case to the judiciary. On the 12th, Zhou Cheng, the secret member of the trial, acquitted He Shaokun and sent it to the High Court for retrial.

Nantong: Riot in Jinsha 103

He Hemei, a native of Jinsha, Tongyi, was raped by his daughter, Xiaoluan, by his younger brother, He Xun. He Hemei was extremely angry and immersed his younger brother, He Xun, in feces. The district office investigated and found out the situation and sent him to the court for questioning.

Pinghu: Citywide Teahouse Strike 104

The number of teahouses in this county is the highest in the province. There are already 137 inside and outside the city. The county government previously decided to charge each teapot one copper coin to cover the regular expenses of the security corps. However, the teahouses did not pay the taxes they collected, resulting in a huge amount of arrears. Yesterday, the director of the department ordered seven representatives from each teahouse to be summoned to the case and strictly urged them. The representatives were unable to say anything, so they sent two people to detention, and five people went out to mediate. Unexpectedly, after the five people were released, all the teahouses suddenly went on strike in resistance. Those who did not owe tea donations were mostly coerced. Today, it is heard that there are still several people who are dividing up the various towns and saying orders, leading to actions to achieve the purpose of canceling the county government's orders.

Hangzhou: Zhejiang Spring Cocoon Purchase Completed 105

The Zhejiang Provincial Silk Control Committee distributed 700,000 improved silkworm eggs in stages this year, and sent personnel to guide the breeding, with good results. The average harvest in the 29 counties and cities in the silkworm area is more than 70%. The purchase of fresh cocoons has largely come to an end. A total of more than 65,000 dan of fresh cocoons have been purchased. The harvest of seven silkworm eggs and fresh cocoons is also abundant. It is estimated that about 35,000 dan of fresh cocoons have been harvested. The cocoon collection offices in each district are now limited to closing on the 20th of this month. The improved seeds and native seeds cocoons have been dried and spun into raw silk by various silk factories.

Changing Relief Measures for Money Shops: Loan Committee Established Yesterday. Money Shop Collateral to be Centralized in Money Depots for Direct Cash Conversion. Financial Public Bonds Allocated by the Ministry of Finance as Secondary Guarantee. Bank Sub-Committee Negotiates Bill Clearing Methods. Silver and Money Shop Reserves Cross-Account with Bank of China and Bank of Communications. 108

According to the New Sound News Agency, following the decision to centralize bill clearing for silver and money shops, the Bank Sub-Committee decided on seven measures to be separately announced to both industries for compliance. These measures have been fully implemented since yesterday. The previously established restrictions on bill clearing for each bank have been abolished. Relief measures for money shops have been changed. A loan committee, jointly formed by the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Banca di Italia for China, and reserve organizations of both the silver and money industries, was established yesterday. Details are as follows:

Temporary Measures for Bill Clearing

The Joint Reserve Committee of the Shanghai Banking Association has decided on temporary measures for silver and money shop bill clearing, as determined by the Small Adjustment Committee of the Banking Association. Entrusted with implementation, it has issued a circular to all banks for compliance. The original text of its Circular No. 76 reads: "To Whom It May Concern: At 5:00 PM on June 12th, the Bill Clearing Sub-Group Committee, formed by the Executive Committee of the Banking Association, discussed matters related to silver and money shop bill clearing. It was resolved to establish temporary measures to be implemented by this committee, as entrusted by the Banking Association. The measures are as follows: (1) From June 13th, all clearing banks, upon receiving payment bills from member money shops, shall uniformly affix a 'Received' stamp and submit them to this committee for collection. However, payment bills from non-member banks shall temporarily continue to be exchanged by each bank separately for money shop clearing slips before submitting them to this committee for collection. (The methods for collecting bills from non-member banks will be announced separately after this committee's facilities are fully equipped.) (2) Banks entrusting this committee to collect payment bills from money shops shall submit them to this committee at the following times daily, except for Sundays and holidays: First time: before 10:00 AM. (All payment bills from money shops received by each bank on the previous day shall be submitted to the committee before 10:00 AM.) Second time: before 12:30 PM. Third time: before 2:30 PM. (All payment bills from money shops received by each bank on the same day shall be submitted to the committee no later than 2:30 PM on the same day.) Banks entrusting this committee to collect payment bills from money shops on the due date shall submit the bills from 11:00 AM to 2:00 PM. (3) Clearing bills receivable by banks from money shops shall be stamped 'Received' by this committee and sent to the paying money shops for confirmation. Before 4:00 PM, this committee shall collect clearing slips from each money shop for deposit into the silver industry reserve depot and submit them to the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications for cross-accounting. (4) Clearing bills receivable by money shops from banks shall be stamped 'Received' and sent to the paying banks for a receipt. Before 4:00 PM, the receiving money shops shall collect the clearing allocation slips from this committee from each bank and submit them to the money depot to account for each shop's transactions. The money depot will then consolidate and cross-account with the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications. (5) Banks shall provide this committee with clearing allocation slips in a timely manner for clearing bills payable to non-member banks. (6) The time for returning bills between banks and money shops shall remain as before, until 6:00 PM on the same day. The procedure shall be for each bank or shop to directly return the bill to the original receiving bank or shop upon discovering the need for return and retrieve the money depot clearing slip or clearing allocation slip from this committee for transfer accounting. (7) From June 13th, the restrictions on bank clearing deposits stipulated in this committee's Circular No. 74 shall be immediately abolished. If there are any areas that require improvement in the above measures, this committee will issue announcements from time to time. This circular is hereby communicated for your information and compliance. The Money Shops Association has issued a similar circular, which is omitted for brevity.

Centralized Collection and Clearing Fully Implemented

Since the implementation of these measures, member banks of the Bill Exchange House that receive bills from member money shops of the Money Industry Association no longer directly collect and clear from each shop. Instead, they are all submitted to the Bill Exchange House for consolidation and cross-accounting with the money industry reserve depot. Simultaneously, member money shops of the Money Industry Association that receive bills from member banks of the Bill Exchange House also do not directly collect and clear from each bank. Instead, they are all submitted to the money industry reserve depot for consolidation and cross-accounting with the Bill Exchange House. Starting at 10:00 AM yesterday morning, the Bank Bill Exchange House specifically established a bank deposit point at its location on Hong Kong Road, staffed by personnel dedicated to collecting money shop bills from member banks. At the same time, the Money Industry Joint Reserve Depot established a member money shop deposit point at its location on Ningbo Road, staffed by personnel dedicated to collecting bank bills from member money shops.

Names of Silver and Money Industry Members

The implementation of these measures is limited to member banks of the Bill Exchange House and member money shops of the Money Industry Joint Reserve Depot (i.e., member money shops of the Money Industry Association, as not all member banks of the Bill Exchange House are members of the Banking Association, but all member money shops of the Money Industry Reserve Depot are members of the Money Industry Association). The list of members for both sides is as follows: (1) Member Banks: Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Zhejiang Real Estate Bank, Shanghai Bank, Four Banks Savings Society, Salt Bank, China Fuhua Bank, Sze Ming Bank, Kin Cheng Banking Corporation, New China Trust & Savings Bank, Tung Lai Bank, Continental Bank, Wing Hang Bank, China Industrial Bank, China General Chamber of Commerce Bank, China & South Sea Bank, Overseas Chinese Bank, Jiangsu Provincial Bank, Kuo Hua Commercial and Savings Bank, China Land Development Bank, Guangdong Provincial Bank, The Bank of East Asia, The Farmers Bank of China, Chung Hing Bank, Hong Kong National Bank, The National Commercial Bank, Women's Commercial Bank, China National Products Bank, Poo Hsing Cheong Bank, China Banking Corporation, China & Foreign Bank, China Encouragement Industrial Bank, China Enterprise Bank, Heng Lee Bank, Silk Industry Bank, Jiang Zhe Bank, etc., totaling thirty-seven banks. (2) Member Money Shops: Da De, Sheng Chang, Cun De, Zhi Su, Yi Da, Heng Xun, Yi Da, Da Lai, Zhi Cheng, He Feng, Heng Long, Shun Kang, Yuan Sheng, Tong Run, Jun Chang, Xin Fu, Heng Lai, Dun Yu, Wu Feng, An Kang, Tong Yu, Jun Tai, Heng Xing, Zhi Xiang, Hui Chang, Ren Chang, An Yu, Tong Qing, Cheng Yu, Xin Yu, Chun Yuan, Zhen Tai, Hui Feng, Yi Sheng, Fu Yuan, Sheng Kang, Hong Sheng, Yi Chang, Shen Yuan, Zi Kang, Zheng Xiang, Hong Feng, Rui Chang, Geng Yu, Zi Feng, Heng Jiu, Bao Chang, Fu Tai, Ju Kang, Qing Da, Heng Tong, Bao Feng, Fu Kang, Qing Cheng, Hong Xiang, etc., totaling fifty-five shops.

Cross-Accounting the Difference Between Bank of China and Bank of Communications

After the centralized clearing of silver and money industries, the New Sound News Agency reporter learned from the Bank Bill Exchange House and the Money Industry Joint Reserve Depot last night: (1) As of 6:00 PM last night, the Bank Bill Exchange House received money shop bills from member banks totaling approximately 1,800,700 yuan. (2) As of 6:00 PM last night, the Money Industry Joint Reserve Depot received bank bills from member money shops totaling approximately 1,310,000 yuan. The exchange house and the money depot will cross-account at the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications. Furthermore, the total exchange amount for member banks at the Bill Exchange House yesterday was 7,581,675 yuan and 1 cent, including 4,313,312 yuan and 8 cents in silver dollars and 3,268,362 yuan and 93 cents in clearing silver dollars.

Relief Committee for Money Shops Established

The committee for providing relief loans to money shops held its first meeting at 11:00 AM yesterday in the director's office on the third floor of the Central Bank. Attendees included Xi Demao, manager of the business bureau of the Central Bank; Bei Songsun, manager of the Shanghai branch of the Bank of China; Zhang Peishen, manager of the business department of the Bank of Communications; Ye Fuxiao, general manager of Continental Bank; Wu Yunzhai, manager of Kin Cheng Banking Corporation; Chen Zheqing, manager of Salt Bank; Yang Jiemei, assistant manager of Shanghai Bank; Xu Jilao, executive director of Zhejiang Industrial Bank; Li Fuxun, general manager of Zhejiang Real Estate Bank; Qu Jigang, manager of Kuo Hua Commercial and Savings Bank; Zhu Boquan, manager of the Joint Reserve Committee of Banks; and Qin Xieqing, manager of the Money Industry Joint Reserve Depot. They discussed matters related to the committee's loan process and adjourned at 11:40 AM.

Collateral Measures Have Been Changed

The New Sound News Agency learned from financial circles yesterday that the Ministry of Finance's allocation of 25 million yuan in financial public bonds from the 24th year of the Republic of China to provide relief to money shops has undergone changes to the previously established collateral borrowing measures (where each shop would submit collateral to the Money Industry Supervision Committee for review and, upon approval, would obtain financial public bonds according to the assessed value and then convert them into cash at a 60% discount at banks such as the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications). It is now heard that all money shops applying for collateral loans will submit collateral such as title deeds, public bonds, and goods to the Money Industry Reserve Depot. The depot will then submit them to the Money Industry Supervision Committee for review and, upon approval, they can borrow cash directly from the loan committee formed by banks such as the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications. The financial public bonds allocated by the Ministry of Finance are designated as the secondary guarantee, while the depot's collateral is the primary guarantee. It is heard that the discounts are as follows: title deeds at 90% of the Municipal Council's valuation, public bonds at 100% of the market price, and goods at 80% of the market price. Collateral that has already been mortgaged will be supplemented according to the newly established measures.

Each Bank Assumes a Portion of the Total Loan Amount

The New Sound News Agency learned from the loan committee formed by banks such as the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications yesterday that the total amount is 25 million yuan. It is heard that, in addition to the 3 million yuan assumed by the Money Industry Reserve Depot, banks such as China & South Sea Bank, Kin Cheng Banking Corporation, Salt Bank, Continental Bank, China National Products Bank, Kuo Hua Commercial and Savings Bank, Shanghai Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, and Zhejiang Real Estate Bank will each assume 500,000 yuan. The remainder will be assumed by the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications. The loans will be handled in accordance with the previous interbank lending methods of the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Banca di Italia for China, i.e., calculated every two days, and every three days on Fridays. The business bureau of the Central Bank will announce the interbank lending rates daily. All collateral that has been approved by the Money Industry Supervision Committee may apply to the committee for cash conversion in accordance with the assessed value standards. It is heard that the Money Industry Joint Reserve Depot has compiled the collateral from each shop and applied to the supervision committee. The committee will hold another meeting today to review it.

Due to the scheduled collection of transaction taxes, which the five exchanges in this city are unable to bear, Gu Xinyi and Wang Yiting were specially elected as representatives to pay respects to Minister Kong yesterday afternoon, earnestly requesting a one-year delay in collection to maintain business difficulties. The petition group formed by gold brokers is scheduled to petition Minister Kong today, requesting a reduction in the new tax rate. A reporter from the Shiye News Agency investigated and recorded the details as follows:

Representatives of Five Exchanges Petitioned Yesterday Afternoon;

The Federation of Five Exchanges, through a meeting of directors, decided to elect Du Yuesheng as the representative to request Minister Kong to postpone the collection of transaction taxes. Until yesterday, because Mr. Du had other important business and was unable to go, Gu Xinyi of the Miscellaneous Grains Exchange and Wang Yiting of the Flour Exchange were specially elected as authorized representatives. At 12:30 yesterday, they carried the petition and went to the third floor of the Central Bank to pay respects to Minister Kong. Minister Kong personally received them. The representatives handed over the petition and stated that the five exchanges were in decline and unable to bear the heavy burden, requesting a one-year delay in collection to maintain business difficulties. Minister Kong did not immediately reply to the representatives' request but promised to postpone the collection date within a possible range. After talking for about half an hour, the representatives felt satisfied and then excused themselves. According to Mr. Gu, Minister Kong was very considerate of business difficulties and was very concerned about the poor operation of the five exchanges. The request for a delay in the collection of transaction taxes is likely to be approved. However, the length of the postponement must await the approval of the Ministry of Finance before it can be clarified.

Gold Industry Decides to Visit Kong Today

The tax rates promulgated by the Ministry of Finance this time for yarn, cloth, miscellaneous grains, flour, etc., are all one-tenth (securities are exempt and not included), but the tax rate for the gold industry is as high as two-tenths. The brokers' association of the exchange believes that this tax is closely related to its own business operations and is difficult to bear. Based on the resolution of the last general meeting, it has organized a full petition group to petition Minister Kong. According to the reporter, the association currently has over 110 members. If all of them were to visit Kong, the number would be too large. After a temporary decision yesterday, Zhan Liansheng, Wang Jiafu, Gao Qiumei, Wang Yingchang, Yu Yuhong, Dong Zaisheng, Weng Nianqu, You Shuren, Xia Wenfu, Su Zhongnian, Lu Junfu, Yuan Jinzhen, Ma Zongmao, Yue Zuyi, Fang Jiajun, and Nian Muxiu were elected as sixteen general representatives. They are scheduled to carry the petition at 10:00 AM today and go to Minister Kong's private residence on Xiai Ensi Road to petition Kong.

North China Overwhelmed by Foreign Cloth Dumping, Domestic Products Vanishing; Customs Tax Collection Procedures Should Be Corrected; Taxing Retail Sales in Sections Yields Less Than One-Third; Dyeing and Weaving Industry Association Petitions the Ministry of Finance for Prompt Correction 115

New Voice Agency reports: The strategies used by foreign goods to dump in our country are meticulous. Recently, cotton cloth merchants have further separated entire bolts of cotton cloth into sections and declared them as retail cloth for import. Because the tax paid is very small, the cost is extremely low, and they are heavily sold in North China, domestic cotton cloth is almost extinct. The machine dyeing and weaving industry association and other domestic goods groups in this port sent personnel to North China for investigation, recognizing the great harm to domestic cotton cloth. They jointly petitioned the Ministry of Finance to instruct the customs to correct the tax collection procedures. The original petition is excerpted below: A petition concerning foreign cloth evading tariffs, affecting domestic production and sales channels, requesting the Ministry to urgently instruct the customs to correct tax collection procedures. It is believed that tariff policy is essential for maintaining domestic industry. China's import tariff regulations are inferior to those of other countries due to various reasons. However, this assistance is an essential element for the barely maintaining the current situation of the nation's industrially weak foundation. The cotton cloth business operated by the employees of our association's factories can still exist today amidst this internal and external pressure, which is largely thanks to the protection of Article 94 of the current import tax regulations on cotton products. This is an undeniable fact. However, according to personnel sent by Sichuan to North China to investigate the cotton cloth situation, the tax collection procedures of Tianjin and other customs offices, regardless of the type of cotton cloth, estimate the price of lengths no more than one meter at 90 yuan per 100 kilograms, and calculate the tax at 15% ad valorem. For those less than half a meter, even lower taxes can be collected. In order to reduce import taxes, foreign merchants are competing to separate entire bolts of cotton cloth into sections and declare them for import. The tax paid is less than one-third of that of whole bolts of cotton cloth. It is estimated that ordinary goods can reduce costs by at least a quarter, and lighter and finer qualities can reduce them even more. This not only facilitates sales but is also favored by the economically backward people of the North. As a result, the North China market is completely dominated by this retail cloth (commonly known as "code pieces"), and domestic cloth is almost extinct. It is believed that the reason why domestic cotton cloth cannot be sold to North China is precisely because of the improper tax collection procedures of the customs. Furthermore, there are no specific regulations for the import tax of retail cloth, and it should be levied according to the same rules as other items in this category. Although there may have been errors in the past, it seems appropriate to correct them now. Therefore, we dare to urgently submit this petition, requesting your ministry to promptly instruct all customs offices to correct the tax collection procedures. In the future, when retail cloth is imported, it should all be taxed according to the same tax regulations as other items in this category, without allowing any tricks, in order to maintain domestic production. This is truly in the public interest.

Two Silk Associations Meet in Shanghai; Improvement Association Discusses Budget for the 24th Year; Control Association Organizes Two Silk Reeling and Sales Committees 121

The East China News Agency reports: Zeng Yangfu, director of the Zhejiang Construction Department, was summoned to Sichuan to supervise the construction of highways. The affairs of the Silk Improvement Committee of the National Economic Committee and the Silk Control Association of the Construction Department have been taken over by Tan Xihong, director of the Agriculture and Forestry Department of the Ministry of Industry. Tan convened a meeting of the standing committee members of the Improvement Association, Wu Shenbo, Ge Jingzhong, Leng Yuqiu, and He Shangdan, at the Commodity Inspection Bureau yesterday to discuss the budget and important facilities for the 24th year. At the same time, he convened a meeting of the members of the Control Association, Wang Guohua, Wu Shenbo, Ge Jingzhong, Shen Jiuru, He Shangdan, Xia Chenxiang, and Li Shuchu, to discuss the organization of two committees for silk reeling and sales. The details are recorded separately below.

Budget of the Improvement Association

The original budget for the 24th year of the Improvement Association was 400,000 national currency. Now, due to the attachment of the Economic Committee, the budget is changed to a fiscal year budget. The first half of the 24th year is included in the 23rd year, and the 24th year will run from July of the 24th year to the end of June of the 25th year. Therefore, the funds of 400,000 yuan should be re-allocated and a budget prepared. The meeting yesterday decided to reduce routine expenses and increase event-specific expenses, with special emphasis on basic silk undertakings, such as mulberry cultivation, silkworm rearing, weighing, and silk reeling.

Meeting of the Control Association

After discussing the budget, the Control Association meeting was convened. First, Tan reported that the spring silkworm crop this year was excellent due to favorable weather and good silkworm breeds. The improved variety reached 80%, and the native variety reached 49%. Although the cocoon price was very low, the farmers' income did not decrease because the silkworm rearing period increased by more than half. Silk merchants also went to Zhejiang to purchase cocoons due to the low cocoon price. In total, 6 million yuan of cocoon money was injected into Zhejiang Province, which is a small compensation for the farmers in this time of rural decline. Next, Shen Jiuru reported on the cocoon collection situation. Cocoon collection was divided into ten districts this period. The collection amount of the improved variety was 100,000 dan (of which 61,000 dan were purchased under government control), and the native variety was 170,000 dan, totaling 190,000 dan. Calculated at 420 jin of silk reeled from the improved variety and 500 jin of silk reeled from the native variety, approximately 80,000 dan or more of silk can be obtained.

Silk Reeling Committee

The regulations of the Reeling Association were discussed and approved, and Tan Xihong was appointed as the chairman, with Wu Shenbo, Shen Jiuru, and Xia Chenxiang as standing committee members. The factories that have been contacted for reeling include Hui Lun, Hangzhou, Yongcheng, Changxing, and so on in Zhejiang, and Yongsheng, Yuqi, Hu, Zhengyi, and Yuchang in Jiangsu. The five factories in Zhejiang borrowed 500 multi-end silk reeling machines from the Silk Improvement Association last year, so their equipment is very complete. The quality of the five factories in Jiangsu has long been famous in Europe and the United States, and it is expected that the quality of the silk from each factory will be satisfactory.

Sales Committee

The regulations of the Sales Committee were also passed at this meeting, and Wu Shenbo was appointed as the chairman, with Chen Xilin, Zheng Guohua, and Shen Jiuru as standing committee members. The committee has also planned to set up an office in Shanghai, with Li Shuchu appointed as manager and Ji Junyi as deputy manager.

Chamber of Commerce Informs the Court That Stamp Duty Should Be Affixed to the First Page of Loose-Leaf Account Statements 122

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Jiangsu Shanghai Local Court yesterday, stating: "We are writing to you to inform you that on the 20th of this month, according to a letter from the Shanghai Pharmaceutical Industry Association, the Da Shun Company stated that on April 13th, stamp duty inspectors came to inspect their account books and found no cases of missing or insufficient stamp duty. Later, they took away more than ten pages of cost statements from the small company, copied from Han's 668 to the last batch, and a cash flow book from 12 years ago with stamp duty already affixed, but with a few pages remaining at the end listing inventory quantities. Afterwards, our manager personally went to the bureau to explain the nature of these statements and requested their immediate return. The response was that the statements had already been forwarded to the local court. The nature of the cost statements is merely a notification for accounting purposes, and they are compiled from individual sheets. Affixing stamp duty to the first page is not subject to penalties according to the stamp duty regulations. The officer's act of taking them away on this pretext is an abuse of power, and forwarding them to the local court is also inappropriate. We were instructed to forward this information to seek relief. Our chamber received approval No. 5536 from the Ministry of Finance in May of this year, stating that if the document is of the same nature as an internal bank voucher, it should be affixed to the outside of the book if it is compiled into a volume, and each sheet should be exempt from further stamp duty. Various report forms, if compiled into volumes, should be affixed with stamp duty according to the loose-leaf account book regulations. According to the regulations for affixing stamp duty to loose-leaf account books, according to the Ministry of Finance's approval No. 927 of November of the 18th year, loose-leaf account books should still be calculated annually according to the regulations. The stamp duty should be affixed to the first page, where the month and year are written, at a rate of 1 corner per volume per year. According to the above-mentioned ministry's approval, for those used for audits, regardless of whether they are called statements or forms, as long as they are treated as account books, stamp duty should be affixed to the first page and not to every page. Since the Da Shun Company's cost statements have stamp duty affixed to the first page, following the ministry's order, there is no violation of the regulations. Accordingly, we are sending this case file to you for your reference, and we hope that you will investigate it."

Sino-French Savings Society to Discontinue Prize-Linked Savings; Prize-Winning Accounts to Be Transferred to Special Savings; The Number of Prize-Winning Numbers Reduced, Already Completed 128

The New Voice Agency reports: The Sino-French Savings Society was established in August of the Republic's seventh year, initially specializing in prize-linked savings. It was a Sino-French joint venture, registered with the French Consulate in Tianjin and the Chinese government. It was reorganized into a Chinese joint-stock company in the Republic's fifteenth year, and the French shares were completely redeemed. It was approved and licensed by the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce of the Beijing government. In April of the Republic's twenty-third year, it submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance to establish a special department for ordinary savings, with a capital of 450,000 yuan. The total prize-linked savings association paid 15 yuan per month until January of this year. From March onwards, in compliance with the Ministry of Finance's order, prize-linked savings were discontinued. In addition to ceasing to accept new accounts, it specially established in the ordinary savings department (1) special installment savings with fixed amounts and (2) special lump-sum savings with fixed amounts. The above two types of deposits were established in response to the request of depositors of the prize-linked savings department to transfer their deposits to the ordinary savings department. The term is the sum of the years already paid in the prize-linked savings department and the years of continued savings in the ordinary savings department, totaling 14 years. At the same time, depositors of the prize-linked savings department were notified to transfer to special savings. However, depositors who wished to withdraw their funds according to Article 22 of Chapter 4 of the prize-linked savings regulations were allowed to do so. The June prize-linked savings will be awarded on the 15th of this month at the Beijing head office in accordance with the previous method. However, the number of depositors has decreased significantly in May, so the numbers and prize amounts will be reduced proportionally. In recent days, many prize-linked depositors have applied to the association to transfer to special savings, but very few have withdrawn their funds because it is not cost-effective.

Summer is Here; Beware of Dangerous Drinks 129

The Public Works Department's health department has issued a serious warning to residents within the concession that caution should be exercised in food and drink as summer has arrived. According to reports, certain beverages on the market are labeled "Orange Juice" and other "Fruit Juices" or "Fruit Syrups." According to chemical tests, these beverages are actually not suitable for human consumption, but sellers are rampant in the market, especially street vendors. Drinking them can easily lead to illness, especially in children. Therefore, anyone who pays attention to hygiene should purchase necessary beverages from reliable stores and ensure that they are completely sealed and the contents are pure. Do not be fooled by names such as orange juice and fruit juice, and do not be tempted by cheap prices to cause danger.

At 1:00 AM yesterday morning, all Chinese and foreign detectives went to Room 37 of the Yong An Hotel and arrested the kidnappers Wang A'san and Hao Shicai. Based on the confessions of Wang and Hao, three more accomplices, including Chen A'jin, were arrested in a thatched shed in Jiangbang, and two pistols and more than thirty bullets were seized. They were taken back to the police station. Subsequently, four accomplices, including Chen Gaofu, were arrested at No. 8 Huishan Lane, Huishan Road. The location of the hostage has also been discovered, and teams have been dispatched to rescue the hostage and arrest the remaining accomplices. It is expected that the entire gang will be captured and the hostage will be rescued. The criminals will be sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation this morning.

Health Education, 2. Medical Relief, 3. Environmental Hygiene, 4. Health Care; (4) School Hygiene Group, collected by the Hunan District Health Office, displaying materials on school hygiene in the city, including the results of tuberculosis tests, X-ray results, physical examination and correction of defects, dental hygiene, and performances by elementary school students; (4) Hygiene Experiment Group, displaying bacterial specimens, vaccines, sera, and other manufactured products, equipped with microscopes for public display of various bacteria, each microscope observing one type of bacteria, and enlarged diagrams of each type of bacteria are hung on the wall for comparison, such as syphilis, gonorrhea, typhoid fever, cholera, tuberculosis, etc. In addition, there are exhibitions on water hygiene and milk hygiene, with a free vaccination station attached; (5) Anti-Smoking Group, displaying slogans, books, and regulations of municipal anti-smoking and drug rehabilitation hospitals, such as equipment photos, treatment photos, and drug addiction state photos. At the same time, a short play on the medical world of drug addiction will be performed. In addition, an anti-smoking information desk is set up to allow the audience to register for smoking cessation, obtain smoking cessation regulations, and inquire about all matters related to smoking cessation; (6) Medical Relief Group, displaying the equipment status, history, plans, and regulations of the municipal hospitals, infectious disease hospitals, Wusong Hospital, Jiangwan Hospital, etc.; (7) Environmental Hygiene Group, displaying all exhibits related to environmental hygiene, such as street cleaning, meat inspection, general hygiene, etc.
