Essays and Random Notes 239

— Qin Wen

Generally speaking, "random notes" are just one type of "essay." Besides random notes, what other types of essays are there? The most common are "various thoughts" and "various talks." Roughly speaking, random notes focus on narration, various thoughts focus on discussion, and various talks give equal weight to narration and discussion; random notes emphasize expressing emotions, while various thoughts and various talks emphasize reasoning. – But this is specifically in the realm of essays. When comparing them to novels, there is no need for such distinctions.

Novels require a "structure." Although after successful writing, it seems like it was a normal occurrence, simply written down as is. In fact, the subjects used in "expressive novels" are rarely true events. Eight or nine out of ten are fictional; this requires a lot of mental effort from the author. From "capturing the artistic conception" to actually writing, a "mental draft" is necessary, requiring a lot of consideration. It must go through several revisions to be completed.

In order to achieve "artistic intent," to make it "simple," and to write it "naturally," writing a novel is like playing with "tangrams." "Moving one piece requires moving all the pieces, and you can't focus on one thing and lose sight of the others." Therefore, from capturing the artistic conception to finishing the writing, it always takes a lot of time. After having an artistic conception, there may not be a suitable way to express it. After deciding on a way, it is necessary to examine whether it is appropriate and whether there are any conflicts.

My own experience: when creating a novel of more than five thousand words, after capturing the artistic conception, I always specifically go for a walk outside several times. Sometimes I deliberately go to a quiet place to walk alone, and sometimes I deliberately go to a busy street to run around, in order to carefully experience and explore the facts from the perspective of the characters. For works with over 30,000 words, I often go on a long journey before actually starting to write. – Although

it is not possible to travel specifically for the sake of creation, those who rely on wandering for food and clothing can easily take advantage of natural opportunities. Under the broad and empty moonlight, in the turbulent rapids, standing on a high mountain, or confined in a small room, the moods are different, and the feelings are different. In extraordinary situations, the senses become very sharp, and emotions are particularly rich. Therefore, some errors that are usually unthinkable can be suddenly realized at this time; and some advantages that are usually impossible to explore can also be suddenly felt at this time.

From the above, it can be seen that making a good novel is really not easy, at least it is very time-consuming. Essays are not like this. Once you think of something, you can start writing right away. This is not intentionally rough. There is no need to construct, no need to correspond. You can just write freely according to your feelings. Moreover, the length is short. Even if you want the beginning and end to match, a few words are enough. It is not difficult to complete it in one go.

With essays, you can pick up a pen and start writing as soon as you have thoughts. You can write anytime, anywhere. You can write one in a couple of hours, and you can write two or three in three or four hours. Writing as you feel is extremely casual! Compared to novels, plays are also like this, really very casual! – Some people also call various thoughts "random thoughts" or "records of random thoughts"; various talks are also called "random notes"; then wouldn't it be perfectly fine to just call all essays "random notes"?

Farewell to the Mountain City 240

— Shen Shengshi

Living on a mountain should be very quiet, but it is not quiet here at all. It seems so noisy that it is annoying.

Originally, the house on the mountain was not my villa. Enjoying the peaceful life of living in the mountains is certainly not something a "merchant of knowledge who goes to the mountain to teach for a living" can yearn for.

Time flies by so quickly. Having this feeling certainly counts as happiness. For a beggar lying sick under a hillside, time probably feels very difficult to get through.

I have been living on the mountain for half a year: when I came from Jiangnan, I was still wearing leather and a scarf. But in the blink of an eye, deep winter is over, and the spring in Jiangnan has also aged in my dreams.

I have put away my leather coats, cotton robes, and lined jackets. I am wearing thin clothes. It is already early summer. Looking at the pomegranate trees planted all over the hillside, they are burning into a sea of pomegranate fire under the scorching sun.

Under the window of the small building where I live, there is a street where some poor families live. There is always a chance to hear them quarreling or beating their children. A fat man with a Yangzhou accent stands there with his legs spread apart outside the small gate opposite my window every day. When it gets hot, he goes shirtless all day. His body is so fat that it is really annoying, especially that big belly that looks like a big drum. I always suspect that such a big belly must have some kind of disease! But he doesn't care at all. He himself doesn't find it annoying that his body is so fleshy that it makes him suffer. I see him standing at the gate every day with a smug look. I have never seen him do any work, and at the same time, I think that it would be inconvenient for him to work! Just his figure alone is enough to exhaust him.

After leaving the mountain city, this fat man will forever remain in my memory as annoying! He doesn't do a bit of work and chats nonsense with familiar neighbors or peddlers buying things under my window all day long. I really hate his heavy voice. When he opens his mouth, it sounds like chopping a big bamboo tube.

Behind the mountain, there are two small schools. Every day, elementary school students pass by here noisily.

From early morning to sunset, many beggars walk past under my window, crying. Some crawl, and those without hands and feet roll past with a section of their bodies.

All kinds of noisy sounds constantly drift past my window.

Life in the mountains is not at all relaxing and cheerful.

I want to write a few articles on the mountain and read some books that I usually want to read, but I can't have a peaceful mind at all.

I can't explain it to myself. Almost everywhere I go, I can't find a place that satisfies me.

I want to leave this place. Summer vacation is approaching. Let me pat off the dust from the mountain wind that has accumulated on my body for half a year, wave my hand, and return to Jiangnan.

Farewell! Small mountain city! Huaiyuan.

A Night in the Old Capital 241

— Yao Mu

—Travel Notes of a World-Weary Traveler, Part Three—

Friend:

In the early evening, when the lights are bright, I ran to Beijing again. Speaking of Beijing, friend, you remember, don't you, the lover-like Beijing, you introduced me to her, and since then I have lived in Beijing for four or five years. There, I also endured poverty, ate cornbread, felt nervous, struggled, like a fugitive, but the most comfortable and sweet family life in my life was also spent in Beijing. Beijing is an aging beauty, whose past grace and charm are still hidden in her eyebrows and dimples. In her arms, you forget her age and haggardness, and from her consideration, you feel her solemnity. When you leave her, can you not constantly miss her?

When I traveled north the year before last, I lingered in Beijing for several days, but it didn't seem like enough. This trip to Beijing was originally outside the itinerary, but I finally circled back, planning to stay in Beijing and then go to Tianjin. Leaving the station, I jumped into a rickshaw with two bright lights and told the driver to go to the hotel on East Chang'an Street. The rickshaw followed the usual route, passing through the stone slab alley from Tiananmen to Qianmen, passing the dark and majestic Qianmen tower, and heading to Dongjiaomin Lane. Dongjiaomin Lane was still deserted at night. Although it was early summer, the night breeze was still as chilly as a spring night. The clean streets and the neat, oriental-style buildings on both

sides made the place seem even more secluded. Sparse streetlights hung high from the center of the street. The lights were not very bright, and the places a little further away from the lights were even darker. Cool breezes blew in gusts, the lights swayed, and the locust trees on both sides of the street rustled. The shadows of the trees moved slightly on the walls and the ground. My rickshaw, the driver, and my shadow swept past the shadows of the trees on the walls one by one. There were almost no pedestrians on the street, only two or three rickshaws sped past. The bored patrolmen stood blankly at the street corners. The two guards in front of the tall, monstrous-looking embassy doors carried their guns and walked back and forth. The sounds of their footsteps could not break the silence of the night. But suddenly, memories mixed with terror flooded my mind. I remembered that I was not walking on a shady path for lovers to whisper on, but in the devil's lair that had been stained with the blood of the brave...

Leaving Dongjiaomin Lane, there was the broad and tree-lined East Chang'an Street. In the hazy night, this most beautiful street in China seemed even more quiet and gentle.

The hotel I entered, friend, was exactly the hotel where I stayed with you the first time I came to Beijing. The old waiter served me with a familiar smile. After washing my face, I walked out of the hotel and slowly walked towards Dong'an Market. It was only about nine o'clock, and the pedestrians on Wangfujing Street were already very sparse. Some of the shops had closed their doors, and the newly added neon signs coldly illuminated the street. I stepped step by step on the sidewalk made of fine bricks that I used to walk almost every day, immersed in past memories. Entering through the south gate of Dong'an Market, I looked around. The stalls selling fruits and groceries seemed a little sparser than before. I passed through the Danggui Commercial Building, which was full of book stalls, and then turned to the main street of the market. The layout and people of the book stalls were almost the same as before, but the familiar faces that used to greet me no longer recognized me. At the north end of the main street, the stalls displaying brightly colored fruits and sugar gourds, and the glass covers filled with piles of golden, oily spiced pigeons, soy sauce chicken, and the like still had a tempting power, but the customers here, like those at the book stalls, were few and far between. Even the peddlers were too lazy to ring their bells. "Why is it so desolate?" I couldn't help but wonder.

Walking out of the market, a few drops of cool rain fell sparsely. The pedestrians on the street became even more sparse, and the scene was even more desolate. I suppressed my inexplicable melancholy and hurried back to the hotel.

The hotel was also unusually quiet. If it weren't for the modern furnishings, I would probably feel like I was in an ancient inn on a remote road. Under the caress of the quietness, countless memories surged, propping up my tired eyes. I thought of my Beijing life of several years, from hardship to comfort. I thought of my wife and children, who were thousands of miles away and missed me. I thought of the old friends in Beijing, who were close at hand but I didn't want to see this time. I thought of you, the person who introduced me to Beijing and left a deep mark on my life... The future struggles and hardships, although I hadn't thought about them yet, these surging whirlpools were enough to make me fall asleep very late, and I had many strange and bizarre dreams, and woke up very early the next morning.

When I got up, there were still two hours before the train to Tianjin left. I remembered that this was the season for peonies, and the Central Park could be

walked, so I settled the hotel bill, took my only luggage—a small suitcase, and took a tram to the park, planning to get off there and go straight to the station. You would probably laugh when you heard how attached I am to Beijing, right?

Going west from Laijin Yuxuan to the vicinity of the waterside pavilion, all I could see were peony flower gardens, snow-white, pink, light red, deep purple, each with its own classical name; but after the destruction of days of strong winds, the season of decline had arrived prematurely, and most of the flowers had lost their color. It was still drizzling, adding to the melancholy.

The tall wisteria frames next to the flower gardens were also bearing heavy racemes, but the color was no longer the vibrant deep purple like violets, but a purple mixed with gray and white. If Beijing is really like an aging beauty, I think the wisteria is the most appropriate symbol of Beijing. Pink and white wisteria sheds.

The vermilion and grass-green winding corridors, as new as ever, I followed the corridors to the area where the teahouse was located. I remembered that the corridors were my favorite place to walk. Besides swinging in the children's playground in the park, my children liked to skate on the slippery ground of these corridors. Friend, you even took a picture of him here once, didn't you? I also remembered that when they lived in Beijing, Central Park was where our family spent half a day. Now, I can only wander here alone for a moment. However, "something is better than nothing," I can use this to mock and comfort myself. (The End)

The Owner of the Knocking Brick 242

— Zong Ge

I saw Mr. Yao Xueyin's article "The Special Use of Literature" in the June 5th issue of Free Talk. "The so-called special use," said Mr. Yao, "is to use literature as a knocking brick." This phenomenon, as Mr. Yao said, is common. However, "the little advantage gained by those who speculate will only be like morning dew, and will never last long." This is what poor literary youths do. I think Mr. Yao has overlooked many other people; some special leisured people; those who will always use literature as a brick to knock on doors! Moreover, in fact, some of the poor youths that Mr. Yao spoke of want to make literature their lifelong career.

We believe that it is not the poor youths who use literature as a stepping stone. For example, in the examples cited by Mr. Yao, running a publication, seeking inscriptions from celebrities, writing prefaces, and asking friends to write book reviews, etc., these are not things that ordinary literary youths can do. And they are not needed either.

Some so-called writers, like certain lyricists, certain poets, etc., have a lot of money at home and don't need to worry about tomorrow's livelihood," and have the leisure to open bookstores, run publications, publish books, and write prefaces for friends' works, etc. What they need is reputation, like the "donation of official positions" in the past. Conversely, poor youths can only dedicate their lives to literature, enrich their lives, and master their skills. Although most of what they get is bounced back, they are not discouraged. These young people who write while eating have no money to run publications – and others don't let them run them either – and they don't know any famous students, so where can they find someone to write inscriptions (or prefaces)? I remember that someone wrote a book, and the cover was from a famous painter, and the inscription was from a famous saying. But can poor youths do that?

Furthermore, deceiving women, getting promoted, and making money after becoming famous are even more out of reach for poor literary youths.

Because there are some women who can be approached without using collections or magazines! As for becoming officials? They can only be clerks, until they die. Making money? It seems that literary youths can only dream of winning the aviation lottery!

Of course, I am not saying that there is no one who uses literature as a brick, but this is what those special leisured people that Mr. Yao did not talk about do – because what they need is only to use it as a brick, just to knock open the door. After entering the literary world, they don't care whether the brick disappears like morning dew, or is borrowed by someone else to become an official or deceive women. They don't care. As long as they already have women to play with and have become officials, it doesn't matter whether the brick remains permanent or not. – At most, they will take it as a "souvenir" or "gift to Mr. and Mrs. ××"!

Literary youths should use literature as a career, that's for sure, right? However, using it as a knocking brick is done by a small number of pretentious people, and not by those who are truly aspiring literary youths.

University Days (3) 243

— Written by German author Storm, translated by Chen Yin

'Look, the dancing shoes have been placed there already!' Fritz said. 'Could Mr. Bolika also be a shoemaker?'

The woman shook her head. 'You know, Fritz, unfortunately, he is a polymath! Next spring, he will even fix your dull watch for you! This shoe was made by him as a Christmas gift for the child and is already done.'

'Then, Margaret, my mother has a large box of good-looking old clothes that you can take and alter for Nellie to wear; each one is enough to make at least three pieces for her!'

The old woman laughed; but she put on a serious face, 'I don't know,' she said, 'that is also not possible; but if the mayor's wife is willing...'

At this moment, the little girl came in again and stood next to her mother. She had changed into a white collar, which did not escape my notice; and I also noticed that the pair of earrings with red coral beads was something I hadn't seen just now.

'What do you mean, Nellie?' Fritz said, while the old woman was hesitating and deeply considering this matter, 'Are you willing to go dancing with us?'

She did not answer; but she put her hands around her mother's neck, said something in her mother's ear, and at the same time her face turned redder and redder.

'Fritz!' the old woman said, pushing away the stubborn little girl, 'Why didn't you discuss it with me alone from the beginning? Then there wouldn't be any trouble. Now you have moved the child's heart; I know she won't let me be quiet anymore!' --

They thus gained the victory. 'Wednesday evening at seven o'clock,' Fritz said as he bid farewell; then, the mother and daughter sent them out the door. -- When they had walked a distance and turned their heads, they saw the little girl still standing there, nodding to them several times, and then quickly running back into the house.

Learning to Dance

The next day, according to Fritz's private confession, Mrs. Bolika went to his mother's house and rummaged through the closet with his mother for a while. Then, she left his house with a full package.

Dancing lessons began on Tuesday evening. My pair of worn-out shoes with steel springs and the new clothes were rushed out for me by the shoemaker and tailor at that time; when I walked into the hall, everyone had already gathered there. My classmates stood around the old dance master by the window, and the dance master was pressing the keys of his piano with his fingers, following their wishes. The female dance partners formed a line, arm in arm, walking back and forth.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

The Sigh of Being in Chen 244

— Chen

We used to have a saying: 'Be filial to parents at home, respect teachers and elders when away from home.' This shows that respect for teachers did not begin today. However, in reality, the hardship of the 'chalk career' and the difficulty of sitting on the 'cold bench' have long formed a deeply ingrained fact, especially for primary and secondary school teachers. Around the time we commemorate 'Teachers' Day,' this situation is constantly revealed. First, the principals of various provincial schools in Zhejiang collectively went to the provincial government in early May to petition for the prompt issuance of arrears and that salaries not be discounted. Secondly, Han Guodong, a teacher at Jiangxi Provincial No. 1 Middle School, sought other employment because his teaching life was difficult to maintain, and as a result, he was so deeply stimulated that he hanged himself in the school building. Not long ago, primary school teachers in Guangzhou rioted in demand of their salaries due to the fact that the salaries for May of this year had not been issued at all, which caused the school's cook to stop providing meals, triggering a not-so-small salary demanding storm. Recently, the education sector in Changsha also requested the issuance of all arrears from April and the exemption of mandatory treasury bonds.

These facts illustrate that the 'chalk career' is already extremely difficult, and it is going to be further compounded by months of arrears, discounts, and the thinly-veiled reduction and exploitation through mandatory treasury bonds. With such a precarious livelihood, it is impossible to expect teachers to be content with education, let alone expect them to make achievements in their own careers. The reason is very simple. No matter how hard-working, resilient, or reckless you are, you must at least have food to eat, or else you can't 'work'!

When primary schools in Guangzhou were in the midst of the salary demanding storm, one teacher once said: 'I didn't expect that thousands of years later, the teachers who follow Confucius's teachings would also have the sigh of being in Chen like Confucius. The chalk career tastes like chicken ribs, tasteless to eat and a pity to discard. For the time being, there is no other suitable profession, and to persevere is equivalent to self-grinding. Therefore, in the current environment, it is like entering an old people's home or being sentenced to life imprisonment.' Many of us who want to revitalize the nation through 'nurturing and teaching' are now seeing that the lives of these primary and secondary school teachers, who bear heavy responsibilities, have become like 'entering an old people's home' or 'being sentenced to life imprisonment.' I wonder what kind of feelings they will have.

Souvenir Album 245

— Mingmang

Unintentionally, I accidentally opened the souvenir album written by my friends from middle school ten years ago, and the past suddenly floated from my mind like a wisp of light smoke. The passage of ten years has indeed been extraordinarily swift, and the changes in human affairs are even more unexpected. A souvenir album pressed in a box followed its owner in travels, drifting east and west, and had long been abandoned beyond the scope of memory, but unexpectedly, in this other relocation, it was unearthed like a buried antique. The cover of the album already appeared a bit old and was covered with a thin layer of dust, but turning through page after page, the smooth pages inside still retained a bit of freshness. What was even more exciting and stirring was that the photos of friends from my youth were still lifelike, and every word seemed to have left behind fresh ink, as if it had just been written yesterday.

It seems that people cannot help but be creatures of nostalgia. When this small album was spread out before my eyes, the ridiculous and lovely life of my youth, or even my childhood, was evoked from the depths of my heart. A lively and unpretentious face emerged one by one from this album, and then I remembered those pure and sincere friendships. How frank, honest, and innocent those friends who still held onto their childlike hearts were; full of vitality like the morning sun, and always looking straight ahead with their backs straightened. How brave and how deeply righteous those people who had not been stained with the grey clothes of society and life were. Relying on their intuition, they lacked the hypocrisy of worldly affairs more than social people, although these young people were scolded by the elderly as 'wild children.' Similarly, although they were not thorough in 'the ways of the world,' they were at the same time more upright and selfless than adults. They made noise, argued, and even fought, but after making noise, they were at peace, or even became closer. They did not engage in intrigue to form a black web of society; nor were they selfish, harming others to enrich themselves. They forgot the past and looked to the future. They held bright hopes for the world, society, the country, and themselves. Without discouragement or lament, they were the most sound and promising roles in composing this world.

However, ten years have passed. This pure and beautiful little group has scattered and broken up as everyone has grown older and their social connections have expanded. For the sake of life, solid friendships have been broken up; for the sake of life, pure and flawless moods have also been stained with grey dots to a greater or lesser extent. The great hopes of the past have been lost; society has shaved off their individuality and eliminated their sense of justice. Even old friends have become enemies, and selfishness has changed the upward nature of mankind. Now, some of these old friends have become social parasites, some have become pot-bellied tycoons, evil gentry, or corrupt officials, while others are destitute, consuming their lives under the giant wheels of society. Some have fallen into smoking opium and becoming drunkards; others have painted their souls with black charcoal or tormented their bodies to this point. Ten years of human affairs have changed into so many patterns, and the passion of the past has only turned into a puff of smoke. Childhood and childlike innocence have been lost, but the growing life has not been replaced by the growing reason to contribute to society and the country the strength that mankind should contribute. Now, this small album is still well-preserved, but into what abyss or what dark devil's cave have those dirty little trivial characters fallen?

This seems a bit unbelievable: a small album has only been dyed with some small dust in ten years, but human affairs have changed faster and more complicatedly than the pages of paper. If this album is kept for another ten, twenty, or even a lifetime, what patterns will these characters become in the future, and what feelings of the past and present will arise? Are people really so fragile and so useless? Is the function of this souvenir album only to evoke feelings? Then I really want to throw this album away!

Sisters-in-Law (Bottom) 246

— Ling Zixi

'What's suffering is the wife of Changgen, these days, hum! Being tormented and scolded every day, it's not human life! Humph, sinful, sinful!'

The words are correct, Changgen's wife has been living in tears and torment every day since her man died, and she has been rescued from the small river after seeking death two or three times, right?

It was still a distant uncle who acted as matchmaker for Changgen's wife last spring, saying that the woman's family had no one left, only a widowed aunt. They couldn't even provide clothing for her, and they were still willing to let her linger in the house? Therefore, they quickly wanted to give the girl away—not requiring large betrothal gifts, just wanting a good person, spending thirty or fifty yuan would do. Changgen thought this was a 'bargain', so he took advantage of the fact that there was still some harvest in the fields last year and married her!

However, in the summer, because the year was dry, and he had carted water in the scorching sun all summer, he stretched out his legs in a bout of typhoid fever in the autumn and died!

From this time on, Changgen's mother said that she was bad luck, even 'killing' her 'family man'. So she cursed her overtly and covertly; and Changgen's sister, Yaomei, because her sister-in-law's family was penniless, fearing that she would eat up her family's resources and take a share of her family's only seventeen mu of paddy fields; therefore, with the purpose of belittling and dispatching, she also borrowed the excuse of 'bad luck and killing people', and day by day, she tormented Changgen's wife, who had already become a widow.

In this way, the little sister was sharp, and the Changgen's mother in the middle was also a 'sharp-tongued woman'; in this way, day by day, a chasm of bullying, insidious, and acquisitive behavior first opened up between the sisters-in-law; and following this, the deterioration between the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law deepened day by day. It is easy to torment a fragile soul that has lost the center of its life. Every day, when vicious words shot out like arrows from the mouths of the little sister and mother-in-law, Changgen's wife always thought silently in tears: 'Living on in this life that is not suitable for life, I will eventually destroy this life.' Finally, one morning, people found that Changgen's wife's body was already floating on the water of the back river, drifting with the waves.

Tired 247

— Simon

If a family is equivalent to a man's fetters, then I, like many others, have used my own hands to put those fetters around my neck, thereby invisibly eliminating all freedom, even the progressive ambition that young people should have. Now I am only tired of the current pile of dross-like life. I can no longer recall the past with a leisurely thought, and I dare not imagine the future. If there is a little hope, then this hope is simply written on water, written in a vague human dream, because two children and a woman's family have burdened me so much that I can barely make ends meet.

Family is really an unbearable itch! I feel this way all the time. What makes me feel this way is the daily habits that surround me.

I am a person who makes a living by writing, and I must always set aside some time every day to sit at the writing desk and write on paper. When I have fostered a little bit of quiet and comfortable thoughts and plan to start working, just as I sit down at the table, before I even grab the pen, the two children start吵吵吵, the older one snatches a piece of candy from the little brother's mouth, rushes out the door and runs away, so the little brother cries out:

'Mom, the older brother snatched my candy, candy.' While saying this, tears and snot smeared all over his face. When the mother chases up, catches the one who snatched the thing back, but the candy has already been swallowed into his stomach, naturally he will be punished with a couple of slaps. The other one sees his brother being slapped, seems to feel satisfied, immediately stops crying. However, pacifying this one and not pacifying that one, the one who was beaten is crying miserably. And this cry is not easy to stop for a while, it seems that he must cry out all the grievances in his heart until he is completely dry, so it provokes the mother to be even more angry.

'What are you crying for, go die, just a light hit and you are making such a fuss, if you cry again, I will hit you again.' But the child at this time does not care about the majesty of the adults, seeing that the mother has no good words, but instead curses fiercely, then cries even more sadly, so the mother really grabs this disobedient ruffian child, and hits him hard, but just hitting does not subdue the child's wild nature.

—Don't keep hitting like that, you should use good words to talk to the children.

I really couldn't bear to watch it anymore. In this chaotic scene, I still want to be able to do things, I vent my anger on my wife for not handling things properly, causing a small matter to make an irreparable fuss. And at the same time, the wife also turns her anger towards me:

—You only know how to make pretty words, why do you just sit and watch, don't you get up and coax them. The children are not just mine.

—Joke, you want to pick a fight with me for no reason again, what have you been doing all day, even the children can't be disciplined, are you waiting for me to do it, then I don't have to do anything either, you can take care of the children, that's fine, but who is going to eat and drink?

The wife seems to understand the unreasonableness of her own words and actions, lowers her head and quietly walks to the stove room. But in a moment, my grief and indignation could not be suppressed, thinking that such a crude life is simply not human. I simply ran out to relieve boredom outside, at this time I often think of being ruthless and no longer going home, abandoning them, I would rather wander around alone, saving myself from suffering this meaningless pain, but in an instant, I can't bear it, thinking that people can't get rid of this entanglement after all, people must live such a pitiful life after all.

Often it starts with the children吵吵吵, and in the end it is the result of a mutual sulking and bickering between the two of us. Gradually, I not only hate my wife, but also hate my children. But I can't leave them, abandon them, because this is called family, and I must always live with them, because this is called they are my wife, I should provide them with everything. And also listen to them bestowing all kinds of troubles or disturbances, because these shackles, this burden, were originally put around my own neck with my own hands, who will I complain about, it's all my own fault.

Midnight in the City 248

— Yi An

Night 249

— Jun

The city has no night, the city is a city that never sleeps, the black divine power of night can never be exerted here, it is always replaced by the golden world of electricity. The bright colors of the red lights are flashing everywhere, boundlessly permeating the entire urban space. You stand on that most complex street, the strong lights burn that corner completely red, and the lights are like light smoke, floating with the wind, sometimes suddenly condensing, blocking the scenery outside your eyes like a thick fog, and sometimes suddenly dispersing, so a street buried on both sides with skyscrapers becoming like a deep alley, stretching forward, cars are speeding on the deep alley-like street, using the front lights that seem to be searchlights, shooting so that people's eyes are dizzy.

The impression of a completely red color cluster will make you unable to withstand too complicated stimulation, and have a feeling of neurasthenia.

Not enough? There are also the sounds vibrating on your auditory system, like the sound of waves boiling, the sound of trams, the sound of heavy trucks, the chaotic sound of people, the sound of songs and strings, and the fascinating popular songs that the radio and broadcasting machines in those fashionable shops are broadcasting as special evening programs.

And what is reflected in your visual function is the dazzling flow of vehicles and horses, the flow of people, the interwoven images of coming and going activities, flashing past like a movie, slipping past.

Do you still have a trace of the idea of night existing in your mind?

While taking small steps, you may already be leisurely doing all kinds of strange rose-colored dreams, and demonic desires are quietly active in your tiny blood vessels, this is not impossible, because all around are some seductive material factors, an occasional illusion, a moment of carelessness, you can regard the neon lights hanging in mid-air as the seductive eyes of women, this illusion is the easiest to occur, in fact, passing by your side, brushing against you are some light soft organic bodies captured with a smiling face and spraying a full body of fragrance!

So you can do all kinds of bad things that you would never do during the day, in the night city, in any corner that is both bright and dark.

And when you step by step walk towards those towering high-rise buildings that climb towards the sky, with tips that cannot be seen, like giants squatting on the corners of the street, you may unconsciously stop and listen to the strings of intoxicating jazz music from above, undulating out of the lilac-colored window lattice, melting into the tranquil night sky that is already late and filled with rolling mist, but lingering in your heart, and the heart is fragile, as if something strange suddenly rushed down.

Pushing you up like a dream. But now it is night, and dawn is still far away.

The Singing Child 250

— Shi Ying

The summer evenings in the market town are not very lonely. Although the shops have all boarded up, the bright lights still quietly flow out from the half-closed doors, shimmering on the dark surface of the market river. The round bridge spanning the market river is filled with people of all kinds enjoying the cool air, draped in jackets, enjoying the southern breeze from the water's surface in early summer. The teahouses naturally have even better business, as if the fatigue of the day is dissolved in the slow conversations and light yellow tea. The child, as usual, dragging lazy steps, pulling the erhu in his hand, slowly walked through the dark streets. The sharp sound of the strings vibrated in the calm air, attracting the attention of everyone relaxing. Everyone knew it was that child again. In the white-hot brilliance of the gasoline lamp, his thin figure and sallow face were reflected, and his little fingers were maneuvering the old erhu in his hand. —The child was not even thirteen or fourteen years old, he was a wandering child without relatives or family, no one knew his name or origin. Since last month, he, like a fallen leaf, drifted to this market town, and every night he sang in the streets and teahouses, and with a few vulgar ditties, he filled his stomach, but during the day he slipped into the Guandi Temple at the end of the market to doze off.

He raised his sallow face, looking at those tea drinkers looking at him with tired and weak eyes, the sound of the strings in his hands slowly stopped, waiting for the tea drinkers to give orders. So 'Meng Jiangnv', 'A Prostitute Sues in the Underworld', 'Ten Cups of Wine', these ditties came out of the tea drinkers' mouths. The sound of conversations in the teahouse gradually lowered, and even the people cooling off on the Guohua Bridge turned their ears and eyes to the teahouse. The lamplight clearly reflected this tiny child. The mournful, sobbing sound of the erhu trembled coarsely a few times, and then the child's singing also broke out sharply: 'In the first month comes the New Year, every household lights red lanterns...' Although the voice was sharp and loud, it was mixed with a hoarse sound, vibrating like a sigh, like an iron wheel rubbing against a cement surface. Every tea drinker was drawn in by his voice. Then, in response to the ups and downs of the erhu sound, he also sang 'A Prostitute Sues in the Underworld', his body swaying with the sound of the strings and singing, as if imitating obscene postures. This further won the favor of the tea drinkers. The tea drinkers almost forgot everything, and were intoxicated by this child.

Page 19

Page 20

Page 21

When the singing and string music stopped, the child seemed to suddenly stiffen. A flush rose on his sallow face, and a wave of pleading shone in his eyes. His thin body moved among the tea drinkers, accepting the coins for tomorrow's life, the tea drinkers also rose and fell with noisy conversations, and a faint sigh floated around. After the child finished collecting the coins, he pulled up the coarse erhu again, dragging his slow steps, and left the brightly lit teahouse, his tiny figure slowly disappearing in the darkness, and the sound of the strings also vaguely disappeared. The southern breeze of early summer still brushed across the river surface... the season was still lush April, but in front of the child was a dark road.

From Guangdong Province 251

— Jingfu

I always loved to float back to my hometown in Guangdong, to that beautiful, serene countryside, enjoying myself leisurely; it was like living in a beautiful dream. I returned with such a feeling. But I seemed to have stumbled into another frightening realm. After only a few hurried days, I couldn’t bear to stay in my hometown any longer. Nursing an excruciating wound, I started my wandering journey anew.

It was the lychee season in May, but I didn’t bring back any sweet lychees. I only carried the stinging impression in my heart!

Reaching Chaozhou city, I passed through the main street. The Four Scholars Pavilion appeared ahead. I remembered the sedan chair shop that our family's business used to call upon most frequently was located on the left side of the pavilion. I got out of the car, intending to conveniently hire a sedan chair to quickly get home. I still thought that upon stepping into the sedan chair shop, I would surely hear the familiar, funny Chaozhou accent calling out "Fifth Young Master." But upon closer inspection, the shop was gone. Fortunately, I heard someone from a nearby shop say, "It closed a long time ago!" I went towards our family’s business with great surprise and doubt. In broad daylight, the door was actually closed. Pushing it open, it was cold and quiet. After calling out several times, no one came out. Disheartened, I turned a corner and saw the desolate main hall and the locked warehouse. Only then did a frail old man slowly emerge from the back hall, gaping in shock. "Uhhh..." This was Uncle Zhen, an old employee who had lived in the business for over forty years. He lamented as if in tears.

"Are you still dreaming? Your family's Siam business closed down last year. This place went under in January. Think about it, the salary I saved up for over a decade was all deposited in the business. Think about it, I've worked hard for decades... Do I even want my life anymore? Go back and tell your brother, there isn't even money for food here. How am I supposed to guard this empty house? You still want to take a sedan chair? The sedan carriers have long gone back to their hometown! There are cars to Shikeng now, you know? Those damned cars! On the stretch from Shikeng to your home, there are often bandits. The wealthy have all fled and dare not return! You still dare to take a sedan chair to look for bandits?" I listened to his long speech, and my breath almost stopped. After a long daze, I hurriedly asked him again, what about the coolies who carried the ancestor's luggage? He became even angrier. "Damn it, there are trucks now! Even if there weren't trucks, who has anything for them to carry? The returning overseas Chinese are gone. The wealthy don't come back..."

I felt like I was lost in a dense fog, confused and dazed. I took a car to Shikeng, then climbed up the old mountain ridge that I used to walk in my early years, all alone, to go home. I planned to spend the summer at home, but the sights and sounds around me were suffocating. Those terrible rumors, the sounds of panic, the nighttime disturbances and gunfire, all urged me to leave quickly. Thus, in an embarrassing situation, I was sent away by my tearful mother.

Broadcasting Schedule Editorial Office

Film News

Ren Pengnian Creates a New Record 255

Ren Pengnian is a master of martial arts film direction. This time, he has changed his style and directed the sound film "Madness," which has been successfully completed and will soon be screened at the Jincheng Grand Theater. "Madness" is not only fully sound but also has bright and dazzling colors. Sound in domestic films is fashionable and popular with audiences. Now "Madness," with sound and color, is indeed a new record created by Ren Pengnian in the Chinese film industry. When it is released, movie fans will definitely be eager to see it first.

Cui Xingzhou Postpones Stage Performance 256

The young magician Cui Xingzhou was recently hired by the Carlton Theater to hold a farewell performance before his world tour. It was originally scheduled to be on stage today (the 14th), but unexpectedly, a large number of props, a small part of which was still left yesterday, had not yet been delivered. Carlton, considering that the matter was sudden and difficult to handle, insisted on the performance as scheduled. However, Cui insisted very much and absolutely refused to be hasty. Therefore, after consultation, it was decided to postpone the performance for a week, to be staged on the 20th of this month.

Miss Huang Yun of the Shanghai Opera Society 257

Kuai Huo Lin Yinye 258

The song "Under the Moon" sung by Xia Peizhen in "Little Aunt" is full of sweet meaning and has been recorded on a disc by Baidai Company. The song "Flowery World" sung by Ying Yin in the same film will also be recorded in the near future.

"Little Aunt" has finished almost all of its scenes after shooting a little bit of exterior scenery the day before yesterday. The screening date is not far away. Kuai Huo Lin will sell a special "Little Aunt" publication when the film is released to benefit the audience.

"Little Aunt" has hired Du Yu for photography. The composition of the picture, the softness of the light, and the liveliness of the lens are all very beautiful, especially the scenes of several night scenes.

In the "Little Aunt" filming location, Xia Peizhen can be said to be the most hardworking. She seems extremely excited and energetic in everything. Xia Peizhen said that the Xia Peizhen in "Little Aunt" must have some new creation.

Luo Jun plays the enthusiastic young man in "Little Aunt." When screening the footage, Mr. Hu Xinling, the director of the Cultural Company, was amazed by his superhuman performance and immediately invited him to star in the Cultural Company's "Parents and Children."

In "Little Aunt," Ying Yin has been an enthusiastic and lively girl, has been a girl who has had a child and became a mother, has been a girl who has shed tears of lost love, and has also been a girl who has clenched her fists and moved forward.

"City Scenery" Mu Zhi Breaks Ground 259

Yuan Muzhi, who has a research interest in art, has a reputation for stage performance comparable to Westerners. His acting skills on the screen have successively released brilliant rays of light in "Peach and Plum Tribulation" and "Children of the Storm." This time, directing "City Scenery," he is using his rich experience and carefully accepting the opinions of friends to study and design it. It seems that in addition to understanding the subtle tastes of art, he has also incorporated the power of scientific control, not only avoiding accidental waste in material terms but also experiencing the pleasure of ease and familiarity in spirit. Yesterday, I watched the opening ceremony of "City Scenery" and learned that the position and angle of the camera had already been marked on the design card. Therefore, the work procedure also appeared orderly and unhurried. Two were still life shots, and two belonged to the actors' postures (a total of four shots were successfully completed in less than an hour).

The Lyrics of Love in Peach Blossom Fan 260

Since Ouyang Yuqian, Jin Yan, Hu Ping, Wang Cilong, and others joined New China Film Company, there is an abundance of talent, forming a strong film group. Since filming "Peach Blossom Fan," progress has been smooth, and work is intense, vowing to complete this great representative work in the shortest possible time. There are many lyrics in the film. When the characters Fang Yumin and Xie Sufang get married in the play, there is a song that says, I love you, you and I are on the same front. Even if the seas dry up and the stones rot, it will not destroy our chastity. Stop lingering in flowery mornings and moonlit evenings. Lingering in flowery mornings and moonlit evenings will make you forget the responsibility on your shoulders. For the survival of the nation, we must engage in close combat and move forward. For the liberation of the masses, we must bravely take the lead. Let the stormy waves and fierce waves stir up the sky. You and I will hold hands, share our hearts, and connect our steps. Only then will we see the sincerity of love, the sincerity of love. It is composed by famous musicians and is extremely beautiful.
